    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17137534099192921238"><i>1814 promises to be another eventful season, but not, this author believes, for Anthony Bridgerton, London's most elusive bachelor, who has shown no indication that he plans to marry.<br/>And in truth, why should he?   <span id="freeText17137534099192921238" style="display:none"><i>1814 promises to be another eventful season, but not, this author believes, for Anthony Bridgerton, London's most elusive bachelor, who has shown no indication that he plans to marry.<br />And in truth, why should he? When it comes to playing the consummate rake, nobody does it better...<br />—Lady Whistledown's Society Papers, </i>April 1814<br /><br />But this time, the gossip columnists have it wrong. Anthony Bridgerton hasn't just decided to marry—he's even chosen a wife! The only obstacle is his intended's older sister, Kate Sheffield—the most meddlesome woman ever to grace a London ballroom. The spirited schemer is driving Anthony mad with her determination to stop the betrothal, but when he closes his eyes at night, Kate is the woman haunting his increasingly erotic dreams...<br /><br />Contrary to popular belief, Kate is quite sure that reformed rakes do <i>not</i> make the best husbands—and Anthony Bridgerton is the most wicked rogue of them all. Kate is determined to protect her sister—but she fears her own heart is vulnerable. And when Anthony's lips touch hers, she's suddenly afraid she might not be able to resist the reprehensible rake herself...</span>
  <a data-text-id="17137534099192921238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1198670182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198670182" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198670182?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198670182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6362303660087856397"><b>Leave it to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn' title='Julia Quinn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julia Quinn</a> to make you fall in love in a few chapters!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496694308ra/22943565.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I've come to realize, ladies and gentlemen, that <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn' title='Julia Quinn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julia Quinn</a>'s novels are an oasis for both my mind and my soul</b>. She takes you by the hand, and with her magical writing she opens a portal to another era, to a world of etiquette and courting and balls and lavish gowns, where the devastatingly handsome sworn batchelors end up falling in love with the smart girls, the ones who are not admired for their dazzling beauty, but can chal</span>
  <span id="freeText6362303660087856397" style="display:none"><b>Leave it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a> to make you fall in love in a few chapters!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496694308ra/22943565.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I've come to realize, ladies and gentlemen, that <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a>'s novels are an oasis for both my mind and my soul</b>. She takes you by the hand, and with her magical writing she opens a portal to another era, to a world of etiquette and courting and balls and lavish gowns, where the devastatingly handsome sworn batchelors end up falling in love with the smart girls, the ones who are not admired for their dazzling beauty, but can challenge them with their wit. And that's the recipe for a <b>delicious, swoony romance</b>!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This Author has come to the conclusion that there are rakes, and there are Rakes.<br>Anthony Bridgerton is a Rake.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The head of the famous Bridgerton family, Anthony, is a womanizer. He's the ultimate challenge for all those Ambitious Mamas that try with a frightening determination to find the perfect match to their daughters. And while his ways of debauchery are legendary, he suddenly decides to tie the knot with the most beautiful debutant, Edwina. There's just one tiny problem; her sister. Kate Sheffield is all too familiar with Anthony's reputation, and she will not let her sweet and innocent sister fall into the clutches of the most notorious (and unrepentant) Rake. Anthony and Kate are at war; but <b>all is fair in love and war</b>, and soon they will not be able to tell each other apart. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But when Anthony kissed her, she felt as if she were losing her mind. And when he kissed her twice, she wasn't even sure if she wanted it back.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>While I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_" title="The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke and I</a>, it was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/861326.The_Viscount_Who_Loved_Me__Bridgertons___2_" title="The Viscount Who Loved Me (Bridgertons, #2) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Viscount Who Loved Me</a> that solidified my belief that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a> is <b>my haven from reality</b>. Those past weeks have been really stressful, and I was in a desperate need for escape, even for an hour per day, just to keep magic alive and give me hope that dreams come true, that anyone can find love, that fairytales happen even when you least expect them. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/861326.The_Viscount_Who_Loved_Me__Bridgertons___2_" title="The Viscount Who Loved Me (Bridgertons, #2) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Viscount Who Loved Me</a> was full of <b>hilarious</b> dialogues and veiled (and not so veiled) insults, <b>tender</b> moments that reduced me into a puddle of mush and <b>scorching</b> scenes that made me relish Anthony's wickedness. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a> has been described as the Jane Austen of our time, and I can't help but agree. She portays in an accurate way the English society, and the marriage frenzy that consumed mothers and daughters alike, but she also crafts strong family bonds, and romantic relationships that warm your heart. <b>Extended dreamy sighs are simply a natural reaction</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383856688ra/6687527.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anthony was a difficult character to like. You admired him for his devotion to his family, and his small acts of kindness, but man! his views on marriage and the way he treated Kate a first made you wanna throttle him! His slow development though won you over, and after a while he gave you palpitations! Kate, on the other hand, was my favorite character! She was extremely witty and protective, and despite being aloof and strong-headed as a mule (or because of it) I rooted for her and her happiness. Taming Anthony, and overcoming her own low opinion of him, was difficult, but they complimented each other perfect. The appearance of the Bridgerton family was also a treat, because it meant lots of laughter, and the bond between Mary, Edwina and Kate was an aspect of the story that truly moved me, and made my eyes tear up.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Love's about finding the one person who makes your heart complete. Who makes you a better person than you ever dreamed you could be. Its about looking in the eyes of your wife and knowing all the way to your bones that she's simply the best person you've ever known.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The story of Anthony and Kate left a shadow of a smile on my face, and a <b>strong and lasting feeling of contentment</b>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a>, I owe you big time!<br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/kat/929-theviscountwholovedme" rel="nofollow noopener">For this review and more visit BookNest!</a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6362303660087856397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1864441877" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864441877" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864441877?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864441877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10559105735853724072">Pure, unadulterated entertainment! I can tell I am going to love this series. The author has a talent for writing amusing dialogue and her characters are all so very charming. <br/>One very interesting thing about this particular story was that Ms Quinn did not stoop to stereotypes. The stepmother was not wicked but was much loved and her daughter and step daughter also got along together really well. It was a nice touch. <br/>The Bridgerton family are marvellous, always bickering and teasing each other b</span>
  <span id="freeText10559105735853724072" style="display:none">Pure, unadulterated entertainment! I can tell I am going to love this series. The author has a talent for writing amusing dialogue and her characters are all so very charming. <br />One very interesting thing about this particular story was that Ms Quinn did not stoop to stereotypes. The stepmother was not wicked but was much loved and her daughter and step daughter also got along together really well. It was a nice touch. <br />The Bridgerton family are marvellous, always bickering and teasing each other but still all very much together. Colin stood out in this book and I look forward to eventually reading about his journey towards matrimony!<br />These are ideal books for reading when you just want some good, clean fun. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10559105735853724072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The Bridgertons are very tied family!!! <br>His only flaw was that he was having some unreasonable fears... but that was quite charming, especially as he was fighting to resist to his wife... and to not develop tender feelings for her...   <span id="freeText9656977723277411113" style="display:none">Swoon. What is it about Historical books that I love? The forbidden? The hidden touch? The innocence? The arrogance of the Hero? And Julia Quinn sure knows how to write a good Historical.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549396776i/27019998.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>

<div id="review_3644920110" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jessica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844580-jessica"><img alt="Jessica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494278516p2/4844580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3644920110?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica " href="/user/show/4844580-jessica">Jessica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844580-jessica?shelf=hate-to-love">hate-to-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844580-jessica?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844580-jessica?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3644920110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4381989520444792453">Enemies to lovers? Sign me up! From the start, I really enjoyed Kate and Anthony's characters. I loved how Anthony was an overbearing older brother in book one and that prologue in this book broke my heart for him. Kate is only in her early 20s, but she's already seen as a spinster and she's more focused on finding her younger sister a husband. When she hears that Anthony is on the hunt for a wife, she wants that rake nowhere near her sister! It was so fun watching them butt heads as Anthony tri</span>
  <span id="freeText4381989520444792453" style="display:none">Enemies to lovers? Sign me up! From the start, I really enjoyed Kate and Anthony's characters. I loved how Anthony was an overbearing older brother in book one and that prologue in this book broke my heart for him. Kate is only in her early 20s, but she's already seen as a spinster and she's more focused on finding her younger sister a husband. When she hears that Anthony is on the hunt for a wife, she wants that rake nowhere near her sister! It was so fun watching them butt heads as Anthony tried to court Kate's sister. I love when there are huge, multi-day parties at people's estates and we had one of those in here! We also had the funniest family game and I will love that scene forever. <br /><br />That all being said, there was just something missing for me with the romance and I couldn't give it a full five stars. I feel like after a little over halfway through the book, I wasn't as invested in the romance anymore and was more annoyed at Anthony for not wanting to be in love. Other than that, though, this was so fun! I definitely love this series and cannot wait to continue on! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4381989520444792453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89783948" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89783948?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89783948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3247357058480536215"><br/><i>From The Cover</i><br/><br/><i>1814 promises to be another eventful season, but not, This Author believes, for Anthony Bridgerton, London's most elusive bachelor, who has shown no indication that he plans to marry. And in all truth, why should he? When it comes to playing the consummate rake, nobody does it better...<br/>--Lady Whistledown's Society Papers, April 1814</i><br/><br/><br/><i>My Review:</i><br/><br/>Well, wow! What a great read. I love it when an author can take me from hating the hero in the first chapter to adoring him by the last, and t</span>
  <span id="freeText3247357058480536215" style="display:none"><br /><i>From The Cover</i><br /><br /><i>1814 promises to be another eventful season, but not, This Author believes, for Anthony Bridgerton, London's most elusive bachelor, who has shown no indication that he plans to marry. And in all truth, why should he? When it comes to playing the consummate rake, nobody does it better...<br />--Lady Whistledown's Society Papers, April 1814</i><br /><br /><br /><i>My Review:</i><br /><br />Well, wow! What a great read. I love it when an author can take me from hating the hero in the first chapter to adoring him by the last, and that is exactly what Julia Quinn did with Anthony, eldest of the Bridgerton ‘children.’ <br /><br />After his father’s death at age 38, and his uncle’s death which also came at an early age, Anthony is certain he too will die young. For this reason he has lived his life, forming no attachments to anyone other than his siblings and his mother. As he’s nearing his 30th birthday, he decides he needs to take a bride and sire an heir. But knowing (or <i>thinking</i> he knows) that he will die young, he has decided to choose a bride he is certain he will never fall in love with as he believes that would make his certain death too painful – for himself to endure. This is where he drove me nutty. If you look up the word <i>martyr</i> in a thesaurus, Anthony Bridgerton would be listed as an alternative word. There came a point when I was hoping he would go frolic in a bee infested field of heather. *Blushes* I guess that was rather harsh, but by the end of the book I wanted to bring him home and love him all better.<br /><br />All in all, I enjoyed <i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i> so much more than Daphne’s story in <i>The Duke and I</i> which felt one dimensional to me – not nearly as deep a read. Both the hero, Anthony, and the heroine, Kate Sheffield, were such wonderfully complex characters that I found myself wanting to truly understand why they were as they were – to feel what they felt; fear, anger, longing…thankfully Julia Quinn developed them so fully that I was able to do just that, and connected with them both on a deep level, making me care for them and hoping for the their “happily ever after.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3247357058480536215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2358170091" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358170091" />
    <a title="Elena C." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68070948-elena-c"><img alt="Elena C." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585853320p2/68070948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2358170091?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena C." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena C." href="/user/show/68070948-elena-c">Elena C.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25322244-the-viscount-who-loved-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68070948-elena-c?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68070948-elena-c?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68070948-elena-c?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358170091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13806215823597128596">Read for the <b>URR New Year 2018 Reading Challenge: Animal Lovers' Romance</b>. <i>(Well. Okay, not really. But there's a fat corgi, Newton, and he's by far the best thing this book has to offer).</i><br/><br/>Do you remember that scene in Fight Club where Edward Norton <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vML5WT5nzcE&pbjreload=10' rel='nofollow noopener'>tells us</a> how much fun Brad Pitt has inserting porn into cartoon movie reels? I think something like this is happening with Julia Quinn's <b>Bridgertons series</b>. You <i>think</i> you're reading a charmingly sweet, witty and sexy historical romance; then all of a s</span>
  <span id="freeText13806215823597128596" style="display:none">Read for the <b>URR New Year 2018 Reading Challenge: Animal Lovers' Romance</b>. <i>(Well. Okay, not really. But there's a fat corgi, Newton, and he's by far the best thing this book has to offer).</i><br /><br />Do you remember that scene in Fight Club where Edward Norton <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vML5WT5nzcE&amp;pbjreload=10" rel="nofollow noopener">tells us</a> how much fun Brad Pitt has inserting porn into cartoon movie reels? I think something like this is happening with Julia Quinn's <b>Bridgertons series</b>. You <i>think</i> you're reading a charmingly sweet, witty and sexy historical romance; then all of a sudden the hero deliberately steps on the heroine's hand and when she fights him off, he kicks her in the stomach for good measure. Now: my reading life is filled with bloodlettings, maimings and guttings. I do love my (fictional) violence: stepping on someone's hand? <i>Puh-lease</i>.<br /><br />Only... maybe <i>not</i> when I'm reading a fluffy historical romance, you know? Or at the very least I'd expect the author to recognize the violent nature of the scene she just described. Which really doesn't seem to be the case with Julia Quinn, who airily writes about wives taking advantage of their husbands' drunk stupor to get pregnant despite the men's unwillingness to have kids (in book #1 of the series) and viscounts kicking young women in their stomach ("<i>Normally, Anthony would die before striking a woman, but this truly seemed to be an exceptional case.</i>" Well, sure. Isn't there always a "normally he'd never, BUT"?) There's just no tonal change between such a scene and the rest of book - which relies heavily on the cat-and-dog relationship of the two leads and on their banters and bickerings... too bad all their squabbles aren't even particularly funny, in my opinion - because Anthony, viscount and rake <i>extraordinaire</i>, always has the upper hand with Kate, the strong-headed wallflower he's trying to win over so he can go ahead with his plan to marry her beautiful sister (don't ask). And Anthony, being the usual brand of Alpha male who would be much more at home in a Neanderthal romance than in a Victorian one, doesn't really have to be particularly witty to shut Kate up: as long as he invades her personal space and breathes close to her ear, he wins whatever argument they were having by reducing her into a shivering mass of hormones. But, whatever, that's beside the point --<br /><br />-- the point being, when I read about a male romantic lead kicking the heroine and stepping on her hand - and especially if such behavior is never addressed, explored or (somehow) explained but is treated as a funny interlude - I just know that no matter what happens next, I'm not going to enjoy myself anymore. What can I say. Maybe I'm just way more prudish than I thought. Maybe some Tyler Durden type is effectively sabotaging Julia Quinn's books by adding jarring scenes to her otherwise funny stories. Maybe Quinn really believes this stuff is hilarious - maybe you think so, too. To each its own, right? But as for me, I'm so outta here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13806215823597128596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2719808646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2719808646" />
    <a title="NMmomof4" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24665574-nmmomof4"><img alt="NMmomof4" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515474309p2/24665574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2719808646?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NMmomof4" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NMmomof4" href="/user/show/24665574-nmmomof4">NMmomof4</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2719808646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9185114553712051142"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was a cute hate-to-love type story with some fun witty banter. I liked both characters, and I appreciated their progression into deeper feelings. I can see how this is on the GR list for top historical romance books. I am, as many of my followers know, a greedy reader though. This ending felt way too rushed and not nearly enough for me. I wanted way more! I wanted to experience them growing their family and the H becoming the amazing father that his dad was! I thin</span>
  <span id="freeText9185114553712051142" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b>This was a cute hate-to-love type story with some fun witty banter. I liked both characters, and I appreciated their progression into deeper feelings. I can see how this is on the GR list for top historical romance books. I am, as many of my followers know, a greedy reader though. This ending felt way too rushed and not nearly enough for me. I wanted way more! I wanted to experience them growing their family and the H becoming the amazing father that his dad was! I think it was a shame that we didn't get that and instead the (very short) epilogue was more about setting up a sex scene and also hinting at the next book. Overall I liked it but I didn't love it, and with my issues with the ending -- I'm going with a 3.5 star rating.<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Kate and Anthony's story. Kate and her younger step sister are finally out in society. Her sister is considered the big catch of the season, and since Anthony has decided to find a wife she is his main target. He starts to pursue, but soon finds out that he has to go through her strongly opinionated sister to get to her. Kate and Anthony butt heads but end up forming an odd friendship. Neither of them can stop thinking about the other and fall in love even against their wishes. There is some witty banter, some laugh out loud moments, a few sexy times...and they get a HEA ending.<br /><br /><b>POV:</b> This alternated between focusing on Kate and Anthony in 3rd person narrative. <br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good until the ending (that felt rushed). I never skimmed and I thought it flowed well otherwise.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No, more like hate-to-love.<br /><br /><b>H rating:</b> 4 stars. Anthony. I liked him. He was definitely a mess from his past, but I liked how he came to care for the h.<br /><br /><b>h rating:</b> 4 stars. Kate. I liked her. I appreciated her sass, her smarts, and how she cared for others.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low/moderate. I shed a few tears, but I never needed any tissues.<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There is a point where the H pushes away, but I'd still say he was the main pursuer of the relationship.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Low. They have some tension, chemistry, and a few scenes -- but not that many and it doesn't take away from the story.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW/OM drama:</b> Yes, but mild <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The H is pursuing the h's sister for most of the book. The H and the sister don't have many interactions, and the sister isn't all that interested in the H. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but there is a scene in an office where the H is kissing OW (that he had sexual relations with before) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The H had many sexual partners and the h was a virgin, and the H was ~8 years older than the h. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This ended rather abruptly with an alright epilogue and what I would call a HEA ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they're married with children <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I wanted more though! Why was it so short and rushed feeling?! I know I'm greedy, but I felt like this was a frustrating end.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be <u>Safe</u> for most safety gang readers<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have the H pushing the h away<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have a separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse<br />- <b>Does </b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_59452477" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59452477" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59452477?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=regency-napoleonic-era">regency-napoleonic-era</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59452477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer517024450510350119"><i>Viscount Anthony Bridgerton feels he’s running out of time, thinking he would die young like his father, decided to finally marry and sire an heir before his young death. When he picks out the beauty of the season, he feels everything would go smoothly, he would have a agreeable marriage with no risk to his heart….that is until he meets his intended’s older sister. Kate Sheffield will not have a well-known rake like Anthony anywhere near her sister! Doing everything in her power to prevent a mar</i></span>
  <span id="freeText517024450510350119" style="display:none"><i>Viscount Anthony Bridgerton feels he’s running out of time, thinking he would die young like his father, decided to finally marry and sire an heir before his young death. When he picks out the beauty of the season, he feels everything would go smoothly, he would have a agreeable marriage with no risk to his heart….that is until he meets his intended’s older sister. Kate Sheffield will not have a well-known rake like Anthony anywhere near her sister! Doing everything in her power to prevent a marriage between the two at any means possible. As both fight a battle of wills they can’t resist the attraction that flare between and the risk it does to their hearts…</i><br /><br /> It took me a few chapters to really warm up to Anthony, I didn’t care for attitude or the way he treated Kate with one part that made me mad when they bit and kicked one another. Although no blood was shed or anyone really hurt (much how children horseplay) I just couldn’t feel anything for Anthony until he started to really open up and show not the peer façade but, the man who lost his father at a tender age and became the head of his beloved family. Growing up with a fear he may as well end up like his father. This is the man that really drew me into the story, although sometimes fear can be irrational, I could really understand and feel for him, as it took a lot to face his demons. <br /> <br /> Kate also helped Anthony face his fears, as he did for her, Kate never backed down from Anthony and didn’t pull her punches, and while at times she did seem a little weak in the knees around him, she wasn’t alone in that matter as the spark of desire flared hot between the two as they both ended up kissing one another or more.<br /> <br /> The couple started out at each other throats, but really grew to understand and fall in love with one another bringing out an inner strength in each other. The steam and tension was always there, but the love scenes don’t come until later and call me prudish or a romantic fangirl but I really love when the love scene is worked toward then the main leads just jumping into bed the first chapter or page. <br /><br /> There’s always a classic or memorable scene in each of JQ’s books and TVWLM wasn’t an exception with the crazy Pall Mall game playing out with a mallet of death and everyone out to ruin the other’s game. Kate showing Anthony she can be just as evil and sly as he. It had me laughing and re-reading the game scene a few times over.<br /><br /> The Bridgerton family is still a riot as they lead a helpful and not so helpful hand to the wayward couple.(Benedict and Colin eating walnuts and smashing them on the desk while Anthony had a hangover was true family love) As always the true scene stealer is the great Lady Whistledown and she always gives hints and acts sometimes as a commenter to the events unfolding with her gossip column. <br /> <br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> a truly delightful read, with a great message of learning to conquer any fears with a love and understanding. Another amazing JQ read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="517024450510350119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16779977362455142685" style="display:none"><b>Enemies to lovers! </b><br><br><b>Anthony</b> is looking for a respectable lady to marry. The sparks fly between Anthony and Kate as they battle over if he can court her sister. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567827804i/28111807.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>The Viscount Who Loved Me</b> is the 2nd book in the <i>Bridgertons series</i>. Anthony is the eldest of the Bridgerton children and the second one to get married. There are 8 Bridgerton siblings; each one will get their own book to tell their love story.               <span id="reviewTextContainer52574452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13565432316166488550"><i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Oct'2018</i>:<br/><br/>5 stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br/><br/>The audiobook narrator was great, and it's still a 5-star read for me.<br/> <br/><br/><i>Original Review from Sept'2010</i>: <br/><br/>5 stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br/><br/>Although I didn't enjoy this quite as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52574517' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Duke and I</a>, it's a heartwarming, funny, and charming romance with an amusing H/H. I really disliked Anthony in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_' title='The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Duke And I</a>, and I thought he was an overbearing, judgmental jerk most of the time. So I wasn't sure how I'd f</span>
  <span id="freeText13565432316166488550" style="display:none"><i>Re-read/listened to the audiobook version Oct'2018</i>:<br /><br />5 stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br /><br />The audiobook narrator was great, and it's still a 5-star read for me.<br /> <br /><br /><i>Original Review from Sept'2010</i>: <br /><br />5 stars – Historical/Regency Romance<br /><br />Although I didn't enjoy this quite as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52574517" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke and I</a>, it's a heartwarming, funny, and charming romance with an amusing H/H. I really disliked Anthony in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_" title="The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke And I</a>, and I thought he was an overbearing, judgmental jerk most of the time. So I wasn't sure how I'd feel about him in this, and although he acted like an indignant ass towards Kate for a large part of the story and was still bossy towards his siblings, I understood his motivations and actions better after learning more about his background. <br /><br />Anthony's fierce need to fulfill his responsibilities, protect his family's future, and live up to his father's legacy is the driving force behind everything he does. He initially sees Kate's interference in his plan to marry her sister as an annoying obstacle that must be overcome, by any means necessary...even seduction! He's vowed to never fall in love, but when Anthony and Kate's animosity and rivalry results in powerful attraction and explosive passion, will they take an even greater chance and dare to risk their hearts? Or will his fears stemming from events in the past be too much for them to overcome? <br /><br />I might not have cared very much for Anthony in the beginning, but I ended up falling for him nearly as hard as Kate did before it was over. <b>The Viscount Who Loved Me</b> is another sweet, engaging romance in the delightful <i>Bridgertons</i> series, and I'm looking forward to more, especially Colin's story in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110384.Romancing_Mister_Bridgerton__Bridgertons___4_" title="Romancing Mister Bridgerton (Bridgertons, #4) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Romancing Mister Bridgerton</a>. (I just wish they were a bit steamier!)</span>

<div id="review_844335931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/844335931" />
    <a title="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18091208-camila-previously-the-opinionated-catruler"><img alt="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460588276p2/18091208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/844335931?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)" href="/user/show/18091208-camila-previously-the-opinionated-catruler">Camila (previously the opinionated Catruler)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749936587" href="/book/show/353066.The_Viscount_Who_Loved_Me">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer844335931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10599515449052432107"><b>Actual rating: 2.5*</b><br/><br/>So... <i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i>. The name itself is a spoiler, I believe. Because Anthony is so fucking sure he can control whether he falls in love or not, and Kate just bloody <i>knows</i> no man, especially a handsome and rakish Viscount, could ever fall in love with her. And so it begins, as I eye roll for the first but not last time.<br/><br/>But let's be fair. I have never and probably never will claim not to be able to enjoy a cheesy, stereotypical and predictable romance. Sometimes I j</span>
  <span id="freeText10599515449052432107" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 2.5*</b><br /><br />So... <i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i>. The name itself is a spoiler, I believe. Because Anthony is so fucking sure he can control whether he falls in love or not, and Kate just bloody <i>knows</i> no man, especially a handsome and rakish Viscount, could ever fall in love with her. And so it begins, as I eye roll for the first but not last time.<br /><br />But let's be fair. I have never and probably never will claim not to be able to enjoy a cheesy, stereotypical and predictable romance. Sometimes I just do, and that's more than fine by me. I really do like liking things, whether or not they're "good quality". There are many things I don't particularly like feeling, but if a book gets me involved, even if that means hating with a fierce passion, it's doing its job.<br /><br />Now, in my humble opinion, there are two things one should <i>not</i> feel while reading a book, novella, short story or any written work meant to entertain in any way, rather than strictly inform. Those two things are nothing or disbelief.<br /><br />Feeling nothing is simply boring and forgettable. I used to think this was the worst imaginable thing that could happen to me while reading a book, but it's actually the worst for the author. If I'm completely underwhelmed by something, I put it aside and go on with my life.<br /><br /> The real problem is when I don't believe something, when I can practically see the author writing it. The story doesn't have to be realistic, it has to feel real. Even if you couldn't care less about it, a story you can picture is better than one that feels forced. And here I found my issue(s) with <i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i>, which I'll address in five sections.<br /><br /><b>KATE</b><br /><br />I can understand Kate's personality. I can understand, even if it is annoying, how unimpressive Kate feels next to her outstanding sister. Her self-pity, her necessity to be strong, her alleged selflessness. What I can't bring myself to understand, least of all believe, is her prejudice.<br /><br />Kate hates Anthony Bridgerton before even meeting him. She hates him for his rakish ways, which she knows about because Lady Whistledown writes about them. She literally doesn't know anything else about him because she lives in the countryside and meets him at her first season.<br /><br />All I'm saying is that Lizzie at least confused Darcy's inability to talk to new people and shyness for snobbishness (more than the average Darcy snobbishness, that is). Kate doesn't even get one look at Anthony and she's already making plans to avoid him and get him away from her sister. And, while I do love Kate's protectiveness towards Edwina and their relationship in general, here it went to a stupid level I could not possibly get.<br /><br />Overall, Kate's feelings towards Anthony felt forced. Even when she does realize she's in love, I just wasn't convinced. Yes, I had the reasons why she supposedly has found her other half, but it felt like a bad acting with a poor screenplay.<br /><br /><b>ANTHONY</b><br /><br />To be honest, I'm fairly new to the HR genre. I'm not an expert by any means, so all my judgment comes from my little experience, but for a rake, Anthony was rather unoriginal and boring. Plus, his humor was as amusing and natural as Patch Cipriano's one-liners. (If you don't know who he is, lucky you.)<br /><br />Alright. It also didn't help that I read Kleypas' <i>Wallflowers</i> series right before this and I kept comparing Anthony to Lord Westcliff and St. Vincent. Because somehow Anthony Bridgerton manages to be the worst mix of those two amazing characters.<br /><br /><b>THE TRAUMAS</b><br /><br />Yes, this has its own section. Why? Because Anthony and Kate's daddy and mommy issues (respectively) took up half of the book. Anthony was all like, "BEES! MORTALITY! I WILL NEVER BE GOOD ENOUGH! AHHHHHHHHHH!" And then Kate went something like, "RAIN! THUNDERS! LIGHTNING! AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAH!" Julia Quinn told me about their pain ALL THE TIME, but I never once felt it. Maybe it could have made a good argument, but the execution wasn't believable.<br /><br /><b>THE ROMANCE, THE SEX</b><br /><br />Both were dull and seemed rehearsed. Since I'm not into erotica and I wasn't attached to the characters, the smut was utterly boring. I literally fell asleep during a sex scene and skimmed through the rest.<br /><br />Although, it was kind of funny when they fought. Before they became pussies and regretted it, that is.<br /><br /><b>THE WRITING</b><br /><br />Here I declare myself completely inexperienced and uninformed for a lot of people's standards, yet this is how it felt for me.<br /><br />There is nothing <i>wrong</i> with Quinn's writing. For a contemporary or futuristic story it would be more than decent. But for a story set in the 19th century, it was distracting. It is clear that this is a contemporary writer writing a historical book. Usually I wouldn't particularly mind (I didn't in <i>The Duke and I</i>), but I was honestly, truthfully, intensely taken aback by it. I'm not sure how to describe it. All I know is that I didn't feel like I was in the English Regency. It was more like 21st century, possibly in the USA.<br /><br /><br />Having said all that, I did give the book two and a half stars, didn't I? I attribute that to the Bridgerton family, the Bridgerton Pall Mall and the mystery of Lady Whistledown*. For all those reasons I will continue with the series since most of my friends didn't really love this installment either. The next one promises to be way better, even though the Cinderella trope tends to get on my nerves, in a bad way.<br /><br />* After some considering, I am one hundred percent sure <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Penelope Featherington <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is Lady Whistledown.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10599515449052432107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer942309593" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10710774430657563683"><b>4,5 Scared Stars.</b><br/>	<br/>Anthony just knows he’s going to die young. He’s father and uncle did, so why wouldn’t he? <br/>So because of that, the only things he wants he’s a loveless marriage just to provide an heir to whom he can give his title of Lord. So, when he dies, his future wife won’t suffer because there was never love between them. (Yes, freaking amazing logic here!) <br/>He already has a girl picked out: she is perfect for the role and he knows that there’s no way he ends up falling for her. There’s o</span>
  <span id="freeText10710774430657563683" style="display:none"><b>4,5 Scared Stars.</b><br>	<br>Anthony just knows he’s going to die young. He’s father and uncle did, so why wouldn’t he? <br>So because of that, the only things he wants he’s a loveless marriage just to provide an heir to whom he can give his title of Lord. So, when he dies, his future wife won’t suffer because there was never love between them. (Yes, freaking amazing logic here!) <br>He already has a girl picked out: she is perfect for the role and he knows that there’s no way he ends up falling for her. There’s only one problem. Kate, her older sister that hates Anthony and refuses to let her sister marry him. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400714985i/9711625.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, when trying to win Kate over so she can allow him to marry her sister, things between them starts to change. Anthony is not the bad boy Kate always thought. And Kate makes him feel things, and feeling is what he avoided this whole time. So when feelings starts to grow between them Anthony knows he’s in big trouble. <br>And how is Anthony will even want to marry one sister, when for the first time his heart beats, his for the other? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388683472i/7901653.jpg" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>Rating: </b> 4,5 Stars. <br> <b>Storyline: </b> Romantic, sweet and completely heartwarming. I find myself cheering from them both through the whole book and I read this in bit, because I simply couldn’t put it down. I loved how their romance grow slow and they formed a friendship while he was courting the other sister. (Well, not really, he never really made a huge effort) <br>I didn’t like it as much as the first (but I normally like the first books on the series more, so that’s probably a quirk of mine.), but it was still a very enjoyable reading. I’m loving these books!!<br> <b>Writing Style: </b> Third person. Dual POV. Addictive, engaging and so, so sweet. <br> <b>Character Development: </b> I really liked Kate. She was a loyal, strong heroine and I just loved their relationship with her sister and how she not for once, acted on her because of the previous Anthony’s attentions to her. (Not that were many, but still.). Probably one of my favorite heroines. Anthony, what can I say? I liked, I really loved towards the end, he was great. But in the beginning, all that whining about dying young and whatever and ruling his whole life and making stupid decisions because of it? Man, I could smack his head with a carrot. And a big one. <br> <b>Steam: </b> Some hot scenes. <br> <b>HEA: </b>	<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. And I just love the “far-away-in-the-future” epilogues these books have.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_698298844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698298844" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/698298844?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Julia Quinn Fans!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=aar-top-100-romance-books-2010">aar-top-100-romance-books-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=british-hero-or-heroine">british-hero-or-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=english-books">english-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=sexy-bad-boy-hero">sexy-bad-boy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=adult-book">adult-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=ronyell-s-epinions-reviews">ronyell-s-epinions-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=julia-quinn">julia-quinn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698298844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer783111925777505883"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379784819i/462361.jpg' width='300' height='400' alt='Viscount' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>After reading the first book in Julia Quinn’s fantastic “Bridgerton” series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_' title='The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Duke and I</a> I just had to check out the second book in series “The Viscount Who Loved Me” and man, was I blown away by this book!<br/><br/>Anthony Bridgerton, who is well-known as being London’s most notorious rake, takes London by storm when he decides that he wants to get married and he has his sights set on Edwina Sheffield. However, Anthony will soon realize that this is not an easy task as he has to impress Edwina’s olde</span>
  <span id="freeText783111925777505883" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379784819i/462361.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="Viscount" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>After reading the first book in Julia Quinn’s fantastic “Bridgerton” series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_" title="The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke and I</a> I just had to check out the second book in series “The Viscount Who Loved Me” and man, was I blown away by this book!<br><br>Anthony Bridgerton, who is well-known as being London’s most notorious rake, takes London by storm when he decides that he wants to get married and he has his sights set on Edwina Sheffield. However, Anthony will soon realize that this is not an easy task as he has to impress Edwina’s older sister, Kate Sheffield, who refuses to let Anthony marry her sister due to his reputation as a rake. Even though Anthony gets so annoyed with Kate at times, he will soon realize that he might have feelings for Kate whether he likes it or not!<br><br>Julia Quinn has done it again with writing a brilliant romance story that not only gives us the best back and forth bantering between the two lead characters, but also gave us a great insight on conquering our fears for the sake of love! I loved the way that Julia Quinn wrote each character in this novel as they were truly memorable and they made me relate to the characters’ predicaments. I especially loved the relationship that Anthony shared with his siblings, especially Colin and Benedict as there were several moments in the novel where Anthony was considering killing his brothers for annoying him to death, but it is clearly shown that he cares about them at the same time. I also loved Kate’s relationship with her stepsister Edwina as it has been stated many times that Edwina is way more beautiful than Kate, but Kate still cares about Edwina’s well being and would do anything to make her happy. Probably my most favorite characters in this novel were Anthony Bridgerton and Kate Sheffield themselves! I have to honestly say that Anthony Bridgerton is officially one of my most favorite romance heroes of all-time (man, I have been saying that for every romance novel I had read)! Anyway, Anthony Bridgerton is just one amazing hero as he has sharp wit while being kind hearted towards anyone at the same time. I loved his relationship with Kate as he often gets frustrated with her since he thinks she is annoying and yet, it is clear as day that he has feelings for her, but often has trouble trying to reciprocate those feelings to her. Kate Sheffield is truly one of the best romance heroines I had ever read as she shows true determination in doing what is best for the people she cares about and I also loved her back and forth bantering with Anthony as she seems to be the only character (other than Anthony’s siblings) who can talk back to Anthony with such fire and wit! As for the love scenes between Anthony and Kate, OH MAN, were they <b>HOT and SIZZLING</b> and I just could not stop reading those love scenes between Kate and Anthony without feeling deep anticipation!<br><br>For anyone who does not like sex scenes, there are plenty of sex scenes in this novel that are quite graphic and you can skim over them if they are uncomfortable to read through.<br><br>Overall, “The Viscount Who Loved Me” is truly one romance novel that every fan of Julia Quinn’s works and fans who love pure, raw romance should definitely check out! Now, I am off to read the third book in the “Bridgerton” series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110385.An_Offer_From_a_Gentleman__Bridgertons___3_" title="An Offer From a Gentleman (Bridgertons, #3) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">An Offer From a Gentleman</a>!<br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2013/09/the-viscount-who-loved-me-by-julia-quinn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="783111925777505883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2580660949" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2580660949" />
    <a title="Rachel Aranda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43622386-rachel-aranda"><img alt="Rachel Aranda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585436207p2/43622386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2580660949?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Aranda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Aranda" href="/user/show/43622386-rachel-aranda">Rachel Aranda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780062353641" href="/book/show/22960618-the-viscount-who-loved-me">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rachel by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/6017923-sincerae">Sincerae</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43622386-rachel-aranda?shelf=library-rentals">library-rentals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580660949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2507064620432635808">I was first introduced to Anthony Bridgerton, the Viscount of the book, in “The Duke and I.” Frankly put, I thought him a hypocrite of the highest nature, and was hesitant to read a book all about him but was looking forward to learning more about him. I didn’t like him much then and I still don’t after reading his book. After reading this book it didn’t fully help my feelings for him but I understand him better. Kate’s character was more complex than I originally expected her to be. Both Anthon</span>
  <span id="freeText2507064620432635808" style="display:none">I was first introduced to Anthony Bridgerton, the Viscount of the book, in “The Duke and I.” Frankly put, I thought him a hypocrite of the highest nature, and was hesitant to read a book all about him but was looking forward to learning more about him. I didn’t like him much then and I still don’t after reading his book. After reading this book it didn’t fully help my feelings for him but I understand him better. Kate’s character was more complex than I originally expected her to be. Both Anthony and Kate have to face their deepest fears and it added a great arc to the story. For me, it made me like them both more and see how they developed into the people they are. This was a good pairing of characters and they brought out the worst and best of each other and that is what love is supposed to do for people. Overall, “The Viscount Who Loved Me” was okay that grew on me in the last third of the book, which is why I give it a 3.25 out of 5 stars. I would recommend a person read this book, if you’re looking for a easy read with a hate to love troupe.<br /><br />I'm not sure if I'll continue the series or not but I did enjoy buddy reading with my friend, Sincerae, who lead the way into the Regency Romance genre for me. I never would have picked up the first two books in this series if it wasn't for her and I appreciate her introducing me to a new author and genre. Not sure it's for me but I'd be willing to read more. Feel free to leave recommendations in the comment section.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2507064620432635808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14729198318512883957">I liked it much better than book one, <i>The Duke And I</i>! It's lovely to see the family cohesion not only of the Bridgertons, but of the Sheffields as well.<br/><br/>I liked Anthony and Kate very much!<br/>Anthony sometimes is rude, arrogant, and overbearing, but he is also smart and playful.   <span id="freeText14729198318512883957" style="display:none">I liked it much better than book one, <i>The Duke And I</i>! It's lovely to see the family cohesion not only of the Bridgertons, but of the Sheffields as well.<br /><br />I liked Anthony and Kate very much!<br />Anthony sometimes is rude, arrogant, and overbearing, but he is also smart and playful. Kate has only positive qualities: she is spirited, smart, selfless, and very lovable.<br /><br />The development of their relationship was engaging. Not only their love blooms, but their personalities are also strengthened by each other.<br /><br />I like the structure of the novel: it contains a foreword and afterword, prologue and epilogue. It is good to get some additional information about the background of the story, and the life of the characters after their happy end. The experts from <i>Lady Whistledown’s Society Papers</i> at the beginning of chapter are really funny.<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText1633421535223240920" style="display:none"><i>"Love's about finding the one person who makes your heart complete, who makes you a better person that you ever dreamed you could be. It's about looking in the eyes of your wife and knowing, all the way to your bones, that she's simply the best person you've ever known."</i><br /><br /><b>Swoon.</b><br /><br />"Delightful" seems to be the word of choice I keep coming back to to describe this series. I'm really, really loving the Bridgertons, this family is full of love and humor and wit. It is a good thing when you leave a book smiling and feeling happy, and Julia Quinn has certainly hit the nail on the head with that sentiment in this series.<br /><br />To reiterate what my friend Holly once wrote (who recommended this series to me - thanks Holly!): I can't believe I've become the old lady who appreciates this genre, but regency romance has certainly grown on me, especially this series! <br /><br />Super extra bonus points for it not having cheesy romance novel cover art!<br /><br />note: There are some very minor hints of them getting a bit physical with each other (not in the sexual way, there is also a bit of that!), it's mostly slapstick, but if this is an issue for you, you may want to avoid.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749907747" href="/book/show/7961903-the-viscount-who-loved-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3641119018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15616118200299530331">It’s annoying when a book starts out great and then leaves you feeling lukewarm by the end of it.<br/><br/>I loved how this started. The introduction to the characters were great. Julia Quinn writes some of the best and most wittiest lines. Her dialogue are always on par and the chemistry between the hero and the heroine is always palpable. At first. <br/><br/>But then they got together and my interest in their relationship started to wane. Probably because we didn’t get many moments where they lived their happily-</span>
  <span id="freeText15616118200299530331" style="display:none">It’s annoying when a book starts out great and then leaves you feeling lukewarm by the end of it.<br /><br />I loved how this started. The introduction to the characters were great. Julia Quinn writes some of the best and most wittiest lines. Her dialogue are always on par and the chemistry between the hero and the heroine is always palpable. At first. <br /><br />But then they got together and my interest in their relationship started to wane. Probably because we didn’t get many moments where they lived their happily-ever-after before the drama took centre-stage. It felt too dramatic? The conflict has to occur - this formula will always be there. But it would’ve been nice to see them in an actual relationship that was established and then see them work through their problems, since the marriage was one of circumstance and maintaining propriety.<br /><br />I still enjoyed it for the most part. The writing is clever and inviting, the characters are heartwarming and I just enjoy the overall historical feel. <br /><br />I’ll of course be reading the rest of the series. The Bridgerton family might possibly be the best bookish family. The verdict is still out there but I think I’d leave my family for them. With no regrets either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15616118200299530331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4212940546358006733"><i>“If I might offer you a piece of advice?” Colin said, munching on his walnut. <br/>“You might not,” Anthony replied. He looked up. Colin was chewing with his mouth open. As this had been strictly forbidden while growing up in their household, Anthony could only deduce that Colin was displaying such poor manners only to make more noise. “Close your damned mouth,” he muttered.<br/>Colin swallowed, smacked his lips, and took a sip of his tea to wash it all down. “Whatever you did, apologize for it. I know yo</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4212940546358006733" style="display:none"><i>“If I might offer you a piece of advice?” Colin said, munching on his walnut. <br>“You might not,” Anthony replied. He looked up. Colin was chewing with his mouth open. As this had been strictly forbidden while growing up in their household, Anthony could only deduce that Colin was displaying such poor manners only to make more noise. “Close your damned mouth,” he muttered.<br>Colin swallowed, smacked his lips, and took a sip of his tea to wash it all down. “Whatever you did, apologize for it. I know you, and I’m getting to know Kate, and knowing what I know—”<br>“What the hell is he talking about?” Anthony grumbled. <br>“I think,” Benedict said, leaning back in his chair, “that he’s telling you you’re an ass.”<br>“Just so!” Colin exclaimed. <br>Anthony just shook his head wearily. “It’s more complicated than you think.” <br>“It always is,” Benedict said, with sincerity so false it almost managed to sound sincere.<br>“When you two idiots find women gullible enough to actually marry you,” Anthony snapped, “then you may presume to offer me advice. But until then ...shut up.” <br>Colin looked at Benedict. “Think he’s angry?” <br>Benedict quirked a brow. “That or drunk.” <br>Colin shook his head. “No, not drunk. Not anymore, at least. He’s clearly hungover.”<br>“Which would explain,” Benedict said with a philosophical nod, “why he’s so angry.”<br>Anthony spread one hand over his face and pressed hard against his temples with his thumb and middle finger. “God above,” he muttered.</i><br><br>From the moment I finished read the first chapter I know this book would be anything but boring. <br><br>It was quite a surprise, because at first (referring to Anthony's role in <i>The Duke And I</i>) I didn't really like him. I thought he was being overprotected with his sister Daphne, treated her almost like a child and not as a woman. I also thought he shouldn't treated Simon so badly. They were bestfriend after all. But Anthony was so annoying.<br><br><i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i> showed us the different part of Anthony Bridgerton. As the oldest child of the family, He carries enormous responsibility. His father's death really had shocked him. At such a young age Anthony has been the Viscount and the head of Bridgerton family which includes a desperate-to-see-her-eight-children-all-marry mother, three amusing brothers and four nosy sisters. He loves all of them so much. The problem is Anthony believes he would die at young age just like his father. <br><br>Anthony then decides to marry so he could provide an heir. He would marry one of the Sheffield sisters, the diamond of the season with sparkling beauty, smart brain, decent manners. She would be the perfect wife for him, wouldn't she? But of course this story wasn't that boring, because there's Kate, the older Sheffield sister who would do anything to keep her younger sister away from the rake Viscount. <br><br>There was one thing I thought a little bit unusual in this story. I didn't understand why and how Anthony came to the conclusion that he won't exceed her father's age. For something that has a major impact in his life, there should be a reasonable explanation. <br><br>Overall this was still a very good romance book with enchanting characters and smart dialogues. Have I mentioned funny? It's Julia Quinn's, have no doubt with the humor.<br>As for the romance itself, while <i>The Duke And I</i> gave us a super sweet romance between Simon and Daphne, this second book gave us.. well, how can I describe the relationship between Anthony and Kate?<br>Certainly it wasn't like this <a href="http://www.smileycodes.info" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/422896.gif" width="100" height="100" alt="http://www.smileycodes.info" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> or this <a href="http://www.smileycodes.info" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/482252.gif" width="100" height="100" alt="http://www.smileycodes.info" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>But rather like this <a href="http://www.smileycodes.info" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365535ra/717654.gif" width="120" height="100" alt="http://www.smileycodes.info" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> and this <a href="http://www.smileycodes.info" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380365535ra/717655.gif" width="70" height="70" alt="http://www.smileycodes.info" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Got the picture? <br><br><i>"Now then," he said, once their feet began to move in the familiar steps, "suppose you tell me why you hate me."<br>Kate trod on his foot. Lord, he was direct. "I beg your pardon?"<br>"There is no need to maim me, Miss Sheffield."<br>"It was an accident, I assure you." And it was, even if she didn't really mind this particular example of her lack of grace.<br>"Why," he mused, "do I find I have difficulty believing you?"<br>Honesty, Kate quickly decided, would be her best strategy. If he could be direct, well then, so could she. "Probably," she answered with a wicked smile, "because you know that had it occurred to me to step on your foot on purpose, I would have done so."</i><br></span>
