        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25322244-the-viscount-who-loved-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26693609-al-george?shelf=03-historical-romance">03-historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1538952260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16870570323667892650">So look, when your life is challenging and you need a safe place to rest, Bridgertonville is the best. It's a break from it all. While I can't say this was the best in the series for me, it was pretty wonderful.<br/><br/>The heroine was my favorite of the two. She's tough, caring, a little wounded and wonderful. She had a healthy relationship with her family....no evil villains there, thanx be to dog. And speaking of dogs, she had a corgi. How the hell can I not love a woman with a corgi?<br/><br/>The hero, Anthony</span>
  <span id="freeText16870570323667892650" style="display:none">So look, when your life is challenging and you need a safe place to rest, Bridgertonville is the best. It's a break from it all. While I can't say this was the best in the series for me, it was pretty wonderful.<br /><br />The heroine was my favorite of the two. She's tough, caring, a little wounded and wonderful. She had a healthy relationship with her family....no evil villains there, thanx be to dog. And speaking of dogs, she had a corgi. How the hell can I not love a woman with a corgi?<br /><br />The hero, Anthony, is fine. Nothing to write home to mom about. He's witty, neurotic and supposedly dreamy. I never got the dreamy not did I get the steamy. But that's ok. <br /><br />What I did get was two very developed characters who's lives went on even when they were not with each other. And that's what makes this a good book. There are two story lines that mingle to one nice and tidy, very Julia Quinn HEA. Just what the doctor ordered.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16870570323667892650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1847489773" />
    <a title="KatieV" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18620847-katiev"><img alt="KatieV" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390618322p2/18620847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1847489773?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KatieV" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KatieV" href="/user/show/18620847-katiev">KatieV</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=genre-historical">genre-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=hero-brooding-tortured">hero-brooding-tortured</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=hero-dominate-alpha">hero-dominate-alpha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=hero-titled">hero-titled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=heroine-plain-jane">heroine-plain-jane</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=heroine-virgin">heroine-virgin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=locale-england">locale-england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=shotgun-wedding">shotgun-wedding</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=era-regency">era-regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1847489773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15022628328402341009">3.5 rounded up<br/><br/>I listened to the audio by Rosalyn Landor, so it generally goes without saying that it was fabulously narrated (still irritated by her voice for Cam in Kleypas' Hathaway series). The Bridgerton family and their interactions are definitely fun and I liked Kate. Colin was a riot in this one. It took me a while to warm up to Anthony though.<br/><br/>Anthony was an ass for at least the first quarter of the story. Perhaps I was being dense, but I didn't peg the reason for his not wanting to love </span>
  <span id="freeText15022628328402341009" style="display:none">3.5 rounded up<br /><br />I listened to the audio by Rosalyn Landor, so it generally goes without saying that it was fabulously narrated (still irritated by her voice for Cam in Kleypas' Hathaway series). The Bridgerton family and their interactions are definitely fun and I liked Kate. Colin was a riot in this one. It took me a while to warm up to Anthony though.<br /><br />Anthony was an ass for at least the first quarter of the story. Perhaps I was being dense, but I didn't peg the reason for his not wanting to love his wife until it was stated. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ He thought he was going to die before 40 and didn't want his wife to suffer after he was gone. Kind of lame, IMHO, but a typical romance novel type of obstacle. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So, he came off as an arrogant, self important ass who had very little respect for women that weren't his family. He wanted to marry some suitable trophy to make a few heirs and carry on with mistresses on the side. <br /><br />I'm only halfheartedly complaining, mind you. I enjoy reading about men I want to throttle. It's an affliction. It was also fun to see Kate bring him down a peg or two on a regular basis. I can understand why the croquet match is infamous. Their banter was quite entertaining. I do think their personalities were well matched. Anthony would have steamrolled some meek miss.<br /><br />There was a bit of a lag in the middle, after the two stopped being adversaries. Also, the belaboring of Kate's plainness got on my nerves. I believe we were supposed to see that Kate was attractive, but her sister was one of those few people who seem to defy nature with their physical perfection - leaving any mere mortal in the shadows. I think the subject was ground in a bit too hard though, to the point that I was like <i>'damn, is Kate that hideous!'</i>. I'm sure that has a lot to do with the fact that I am not a huge fan of the 'plain Jane' heroine trope, YMMV. <br /><br />Enjoyable series from what I've read. Like the Hathaways, a lot of the enjoyment comes from the family dynamics and bickering/teasing siblings. Most definitely a good palate cleanser after some dark urban fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15022628328402341009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XABAfatJ3356lsfgPS8acrHScXFlQ4DpQUm1P8Wt/fJoes1WUK1Hd2jdSo8WuHA3DUoM2kCRwk2XJnmj+q/bTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tUmqF8Y3AFvq/zJGjKIPCjneMiQMErhoRPMtCbB2rbyBMyc8PdOYUvi0vymnNWVPhUZPjynA+sySnOGVj3SLAg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14140139887504649729">#1 New York Times bestselling author Julia Quinn loves to dispel the myth that smart women don't read (or write) romance, and and if you watch reruns of the game show The Weakest Link you might just catch her winning the $79,000 jackpot. She displayed a decided lack of knowledge about baseball, country music, and plush toys, but she is proud to say that she aced all things British and literary, an</span>
  <span id="freeText14140139887504649729" style="display:none">#1 New York Times bestselling author Julia Quinn loves to dispel the myth that smart women don't read (or write) romance, and and if you watch reruns of the game show The Weakest Link you might just catch her winning the $79,000 jackpot. She displayed a decided lack of knowledge about baseball, country music, and plush toys, but she is proud to say that she aced all things British and literary, answered all of her history and geography questions correctly, and knew that there was a Da Vinci long before there was a code.<br /><br />A graduate of Harvard and Radcliffe Colleges, Ms. Quinn is one of only sixteen members of Romance Writers of America’s Hall of Fame. Her books have been translated into 32 languages, and she lives with her family in the Pacific Northwest.<br /><br />The Bridgertons, her popular series of historical romance, is currently in production by Shondaland as a Netflix original series starring Julie Andrews, Phoebe Dynevor, and Rége-Jean Page.</span>
